## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (single-species population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate modeled as an ODE driven by the current population P and possibly time t (environmental forcing, interventions). Common structures encode per-capita growth, density dependence (crowding/competition), depensation (Allee effects), harvesting, and seasonality.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; constant per-capita rate)
- Exponential growth with immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (stocking/immigration adds a baseline influx)
- Linear birthŌĆōdeath balance: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net growth as difference of per-capita birth and death rates)
- Density-dependent (Verhulst-type) quadratic crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (competition reduces growth at high P)
- Generalized density dependence (theta-logistic / power crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**(c2) (nonlinear crowding stronger/weaker than quadratic)
- Carrying-capacity form (equivalent re-parameterization): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (growth slows linearly with P toward a capacity)
- Richards / generalized logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal approach; shape controlled by c2)
- Gompertz-type regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines with log of crowding; asymmetric sigmoid)
- Allee effect (depensation) with crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (reduced growth at low P plus high-P limitation)
- Proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net growth with constant fraction removed per unit time)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 (fixed quota removal; can drive extinction at low P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita rate)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))) (resource capacity fluctuates over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Model per-capita growth explicitly: (dP_dt) / P isolates mechanisms; constants in that quantity suggest density-independent growth, while dependence on P indicates regulation.
- Negative P**2 (or higher power) terms typically represent competition/crowding; the power controls how sharply growth collapses at high P.
- Factors of the form (1 - c * P) imply a finite carrying capacity; the zero-crossing of dP_dt gives an equilibrium population size.
- log(c / P) in the per-capita term is characteristic of Gompertz regulation (growth depends on multiplicative distance to capacity rather than additive distance).
- An extra low-population factor like (c * P - 1) indicates an Allee threshold: dP_dt can be negative when P is below a critical level.
- Additive constants (┬▒c) in dP_dt indicate external sources/sinks (immigration/stocking vs constant-yield harvesting) that do not scale with P.
- Time-periodic terms sin(c*t + c0) multiplying P suggest seasonal forcing (birth rate, mortality, or resources varying annually).
- If coefficients depend on t (e.g., c0 + c1*t, or c0 + c1*sin(c2*t)), interpret as changing environment, management interventions, or long-term trends in vital rates.

\[
0.8770002846\,P\sin(0.5671736066\,t)\;+\;0.7013915187(1-P/65.75413114)P
\]
Expand the quadratic part:
\[
0.7013915187\,P\;-\;\frac{0.7013915187}{65.75413114}P^2
\]
So GT has exactly these components (and nothing else):
- a **\(P^2\)** term with coefficient \(-0.7013915187/65.75413114\)
- a **\(P\)** term with coefficient \(+0.7013915187\)
- a **\(P\sin(\omega t)\)** term with amplitude \(0.8770002846\) and frequency \(\omega=0.5671736066\)
- **no constants**, no other functions (no cos, sqrt, abs, max, log, exp, rational terms, extra sin terms, etc.)

Now check candidates for whether their free constants can be set to reproduce exactly \(aP^2 + bP + dP\sin(\omega t)\).

### 1. `P**2*c0 + P*c1*sin(c2 + c3*t) + P*c4`
Form matches \(P^2\) + \(P\sin(\cdot)\) + \(P\). Choose:

- \(c1 = 0.8770002846\)
- need \(\sin(c2+c3 t)=\sin(0.5671736066\,t)\) for all \(t\). This is achievable with \(c3=0.5671736066\) and \(c2=0\) (or \(2\pi k\)).
- \(c4 = 0.7013915187\)

Ō£ģ Can match GT.

### 2. `P**2*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4*cos(c5*t + c6)`

### 3. `P*c0 + P*c1*(P*c2)**c3 + P*c4 + P*c5*sin(c6*t + c7)`
The middle term is \(P*c1*(P*c2)^{c3} = c1*c2^{c3} * P^{c3+1}\). To get a \(P^2\) term, set \(c3=1\), giving \( \propto P^2\). Then we can combine \(P*c0 + P*c4\) into the linear term, and the sine term matches.

- \(c3=1\)
- \(c1*c2 = -0.7013915187/65.75413114\) (many solutions)
- \(c0+c4 = 0.7013915187\)
- \(c5=0.8770002846,\; c6=0.5671736066,\; c7=0\)

Ō£ģ Can match GT.

- \(c1+c2 = 0.7013915187\)
- \(c3=0.8770002846,\; c4=0.5671736066,\; c5=0\)

Ō£ģ Can match GT.

### 11. `P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*Max(0, c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + 1)`
The `Max` creates a piecewise non-sinusoidal shape unless the inside is always Ōēź0 and linear in sin; even then it becomes \(P*c2*(c3\sin(\cdot)+1)\) only if always positive. But to guarantee always positive for all t, need \(|c3|\le 1\) and shift 1; still yields \(P\) and \(P\sin\) terms, so potentially workable. However it also forces the coefficient of the constant-in-time part inside Max to be exactly 1 (times \(c2\)), which is okay. We can ensure positivity by choosing \(c3=0\), but then sine vanishes (bad). If choose \(c3\neq 0\) with \(|c3|\le 1\), expression equals \(P*c2*(1+c3\sin(\cdot))\) for all t (since always Ōēź0). Then we can match \(P\) and \(P\sin\). Quadratic term from \(P^2*c0\) matches too.
So choose:
- \(c0=-0.7013915187/65.75413114\)
- \(c2=0.7013915187\) and \(c2*c3=0.8770002846\) ŌćÆ \(c3=0.8770002846/0.7013915187\approx 1.2509\), but this violates \(|c3|\le 1\) needed to keep \(1+c3\sin\) nonnegative for all t. If \(|c3|>1\), Max clips part of the cycle, not equal to sine.
Could instead use \(P*c1\) to help linear term, but the sine amplitude still comes only from \(P*c2*Max(...)\) and is clipped unless \(|c3|\le 1\). With \(|c3|\le 1\), max sine amplitude is at most \(c2\), and also \(c2*c3\) bounded by \(|c2|\). You could set \(c2\) large and \(c3\) small to get product 0.877 while keeping \(|c3|\le 1\); but then the linear term contributed by this block is \(P*c2\), which would be too large unless canceled by \(P*c1\) (allowed). Yet positivity requires \(1+c3\sin\ge 0\) which holds if \(|c3|\le 1\), independent of \(c2\). Great: pick \(c3=1\), then need \(c2=0.8770002846\) for sine amplitude, and then linear from this block is \(0.8770002846 P\), which can be adjusted with \(P*c1\) to reach 0.7013915187. Set \(c1 = 0.7013915187-0.8770002846\) (negative). This works and Max never clips because \(1+\sin\ge 0\).
Also set \(c4=0.5671736066,\; c5=0\).

Ō£ģ Can match GT.
